Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what happens to the substrate when something emerges from potentiality to actuality, as in the example of the sperm?
A) The substrate becomes stronger.
B) The substrate perishes or changes.
C) The substrate continues to exist unchanged.
D) The substrate becomes the actual thing.

Key Takeaway
The hyle theory fails because potential existence always leads to the perishing of the substrate, so hyle cannot be an eternal origin of the world.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just learned that when potential becomes actual, the original substrate perishes. What 'potential' are you holding onto in your life—a good deed you keep postponing, a repentance you delay—thinking it can stay safe indefinitely? When will you let it become actual, knowing that the moment of delay itself perishes?
?
The hyle theorists sought an eternal origin to avoid acknowledging that everything (including their own existence) is contingent upon Allah. What 'eternal safety net' do you rely on in your heart—your health, youth, wealth, or even your own good deeds—as if it were truly permanent? How does this lesson expose that trust as misplaced?
?
If every substrate perishes when its potential is actualized, then every moment you do not act on your intention to obey Allah, that potential dies. Look at your last week: how many intentions to pray on time, to lower your gaze, to give charity never became actual? What do you think that says about the state of your heart's 'hyle'? Will you let today's intention perish too?

Refuting the Qaramitah's First Originated Being
Maturidi refutes Qaramitah cosmology by applying the potentiality-perishability argument and noting the imperceptibility of the first being.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's refutation of the Qaramitah claim that the first originated being contains the world potentially, and his argument that such a being would perish like all potential things.

Core Idea
The Qaramitah's first originated being, if it contains the world potentially, would perish when the world becomes actual.

Maturidi extends his critique to the Qaramitah, who believe in a first originated being (al-mubdi' al-awwal) that contains the whole world potentially. From that being, the universal soul derives and supplies hyle, leading to the composition of the world. Maturidi applies the same logic: if the world was in the first being potentially, then that first being must perish when the world emerges actually, just like all other potential things. He also notes that the first being (the whole) is known only through its parts and is imperceptible, further undermining its alleged primacy.

Guided Path
1
Read the Qaramitah passage
Read the Arabic text from 'وكذلك يلزم القرامطة' to the end, along with the translation.
Notice how Maturidi connects the Qaramitah view to the same potentiality problem.
2
Understand the Qaramitah view
The Qaramitah say the first originated being (al-mubdi' al-awwal) contains the world potentially, the universal soul derives from it, and the soul supplies hyle.
This is a complex emanationist cosmology.
3
Apply the potentiality critique
Maturidi argues that since the world is in the first being potentially, the first being must perish when the world becomes actual, just like other potential substrates. Thus the first being cannot be eternal.
The conclusion: 'أن يتلف الأول'.
4
Note the epistemological point
Maturidi adds that the first being (the whole) is known only through its parts (the world) and is imperceptible, undermining any claim to know it directly.
This reinforces the argument that the first being is not self-sufficient.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ما يلحق العالم ويظهر جوهرها عجزها وحاجاتها ، وهما دليلا حدث العالم وكونه فيلزم فيها ما يلزم فى غيرها ، أو كانت خارجة من هذا الجوهر غنية قوية بغيره ، لا تمسها الحاجات ولا يعترضها الشهوات الباعثة على الحيل المفزعة إلى تأمل غناها وقوتها ، فأما إن كان العالم بها بأن اعترضت بها العوارض وانقلبت بجوهرها عما كانت عليه فصارت إلى هذه الحاجات والشهوات ، فصارت بجوهرها محتملة لكل حاجة ، محتملة لكل شهوة ، متمكنة للاستحالة والتغير ، فيبطل عنها جميع أوصاف الغنى والقوة ، وصارت أصل الحاجات وأم الشهوات ، فلزم انصراف تدبيرها إلى حكيم عليم ، على ما لزم ذلك في جميع العالم ، أو كانت هي بحالها، لكن العالم كان فيها بقوة ، ظهر بالفعل ، وذلك هو قول أصحاب الهيولى ، ثم دل تلف جميع ما في العالم من كون شيء في شيء بالقوة إذا خرج منه بالفعل نحو ما يقولون من كون النسمة في النطقة ، وكل حيوان في النطف أو البيض ، والعصف في الحب ، والشجر فى النواة ، وكذلك كل الجواهر ، ومثله عندهم البقاء في الأغذية والنماء ونحو ذلك ، فيجب أن يكون أمر الطينة التي قالوا بها وأمر الهيولى كذلك ؛ إذ هما الأصل لجميع العالم .. وكذلك يلزم القرامطة - في قولهم إن المبدع الأول فيه جميع العالم مبروزا تستمد منه النَّفْس الكل فيمد الهيولى ومنه تركيب العالم - أن يتلف الأول ؛ إذ هذا حق كل شيء في شيء بالقوة يظهر بالفعل وقد صيروا جميعا الوجود للحال دليل الأولية ، لكن الأول جوهر الكل والثانى جوهر الجزء ، وقد صار جوهر الكل معروفا بجوهر الجزء ؛ إذ ليس مما يبلغه أحد بالحس ، وبالله التوفيق .
What attaches to the world and reveals the incapacity and needs of its substance (jawhar) — these are the two proofs of the world's origination (huduth) and its existence, so what is necessary in other things is necessary in it. Or [the substance] is outside this substance, rich and strong by other than itself, needs do not touch it, nor do desires that drive to devices making one rush to contemplate its richness and strength. But if the world is by it [the substance] in that accidents affect it and it is changed in its substance from what it was, and so it becomes subject to these needs and desires, then by its substance it becomes susceptible to every need, susceptible to every desire, capable of change and alteration, then all attributes of richness and strength are voided for it, and it becomes the source of needs and the mother of desires. So its governance must be directed to a wise, knowledgeable (Creator), as that is necessary in the whole world. Or [the substance] is as it is, but the world was in it potentially, and appeared actually — that is the saying of the proponents of hyle (ashab al-hayula). Then the perishing of all that is in the world from something being in something potentially, when it emerges from it actually, indicates — like their saying of the soul being in the sperm, every animal in sperm or eggs, the bird in the egg, the tree in the seed, and likewise all substances, and similarly according to them preservation in foods and growth and the like. So it must be that the matter of the clay (al-tina) they spoke of and the matter of hyle are likewise, since they are the origin of the whole world. Similarly, it is necessary for the Qaramitah — in their saying that the first originated being (al-mubdi' al-awwal) contains the whole world potentially, the universal soul derives from it, it furnishes hyle, and from it the composition of the world — that the first should perish, since this is the truth of everything that is in something potentially and appears actually. And they all made existence a proof of primacy (al-awwaliyya) at the moment, but the first is the substance of the whole, and the second is the substance of the part, and the substance of the whole is known by the substance of the part, since it is not something that anyone can perceive by sense. And with God is success.
Source pages p. 662

Commentary
This passage is a multi-part argument about the nature of the world's substance (jawhar) and its implications for the existence of a wise Creator, while refuting the theories of hyle and the Qaramitah. The author first presents a disjunction: either the world's substance is inherently weak and needy, which proves its origination and need for a Creator, or it is independent and strong, which would exempt it from needs. But observation shows the substance is subject to accidents and change, proving it is needy. Therefore, its governance must come from a wise, knowledgeable being. The author then addresses the view of 'ashab al-hayula (proponents of prime matter) who claim the world existed potentially in a substrate and appeared actually. He argues that since everything that exists potentially eventually perishes (as seen in sperm, seeds, etc.), the primordial substrate (hyle or clay) would also be perishable. He extends the same critique to the Qaramitah, who claim the first originated being contains the whole world potentially, and that the world emerges from it. If so, the first must perish like all potential things. The author concludes by noting that they all make existence evidence of primacy, but the first (the whole) is unknowable in itself, known only through its parts, and ultimately inaccessible to sense. The passage is a dense argument combining contingency, potentiality, and refutation of rival views.

Key Terms
القرامطة (al-Qaramitah)
المبدع الأول (al-mubdi' al-awwal, the first originated being)
النَّفْس الكل (al-nafs al-kull, the universal soul)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the Qaramitah view avoids the problem because the first being is spiritual, but Maturidi shows that the same law of potentiality applies universally.
Correction: Even if the first being is non-material, the principle that potential existence leads to perishing of the substrate still holds, as Maturidi applies it to the Qaramitah's first being.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, why must the Qaramitah's first originated being perish?
A) Because it is composed of parts.
B) Because it contains the world potentially, and all potential things cause the substrate to perish when actualized.
C) Because the universal soul consumes it.
D) Because it is made of hyle.

Key Takeaway
The Qaramitah's first originated being, containing the world potentially, would necessarily perish like all potential substrates, and it remains unknowable through the senses.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This passage argues that anything existing potentially perishes when actualized. What is something in your own life—a skill, relationship, or ambition—that you hold only as a potential? If it becomes actual, are you prepared for what it might cost you? Will you cling to it or let it be transformed?
?
The Qaramitah claimed the first being is known through the existence of the world, but Maturidi says it is imperceptible. Have you ever assumed you understood God based solely on what you can see and sense? How might this passage expose a hidden reliance on sensory proof in your own faith? Commit today to seeking knowledge of the unseen through revelation and reason, not mere observation.

Contingency and Refutation of Eternal Potentiality
Maturidi establishes contingency and refutes Qaramitah potentiality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi establishes that all contingent events point to a contingent origin and why the Qaramitah view of an eternal origin with potentiality is self-defeating.

Core Idea
If the origin contained all things potentially, then nothing could be known for certain.

Maturidi continues his argument for tawhid by examining the implications of contingency. He argues that if the world is made up of contingent events, then the origin itself must be contingent and could not be eternal as the Qaramitah claim. Moreover, their model of potentiality actually leads to ignorance.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Note the logical flow from contingency to refutation.
The passage is dense—slow down and follow each claim.
2
Identify the two key claims
Identify Maturidi's claim that the origin is contingent and the Qaramitah claim of an eternal origin. Notice how he uses the concept of potentiality to refute them.
Look for the phrase 'القوة' (potentiality) and its implication.
3
Understand the example of sperms and seeds
Maturidi uses the analogy of sperms and seeds to show that potentiality implies ignorance of future states. Reflect on why this applies to hyle and clay as well.
This example illustrates the absurdity of the Qaramitah view.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Conclude that the Qaramitah claim lacks governance (تدبير) and is invalid. Ask yourself: Why does potentiality lead to ignorance?
This step solidifies the refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأدلة وإذا ثبت هذا ثبت جميع ما بيننا من الحوادث والحاجات التي هي للحدث لذلك الأصل؛ إذ صار محتملا للتلف والفناء، وذلك أيضا يلزم القرامطة يجعلونه أبديا، وإن كانوا يقولون : كان بعد أن لم يكن بالإبداع، ولا قوة إلا بالله ودليل الجهل تمن فيه ما فيه بالقوة بأحوال ما فيه ومن فيه وما يكون ذكرت من جهل النطف والحبوب وغيرها، فيلزم كذلك في الهيولى والطينة وما قالوا، ولزم أن ليس لما قالوا تدبير، ولا كان شيء من ذلك به، ولكن إن كان فهو يمن علم ما يكون فيجعل أصله مبروزا فيه بالقوة، يظهر بالفعل بما جعل له من المواد والأمكنة التي بها تنمو في ذلك القول بالتوحيد، وأنه منشى ذلك كله ليكون به كل شيء يكون على ما قالوا، أو أن يكون محدثا لكل شيء يكون أبدا على ما يشاء أن يكون من أصول وابتداء، أو كيف شاء على ما يقوله أهل التوحيد. وإذ الله سبحانه قادر على إنشاء أصل فيه كل شيء مبروزا، هو قادر على ابتداء كل شيء كما شاء من غير بروز بالقوة ولا خروج بالفعل، ولكن بالتقدير والتكوين . وإن زعموا أن الأشياء كانت في الأصل مستجنّة بجوهرها فيظهر بالفعل فهي أيضا ترجع إلى ما قلنا؛ لأن ذلك قولهم فى النطف والحبوب، مع ما في هذا مما في العقل دفعه بما لا يحتمل تمكن أضعاف الشيء بجوهره فيه؛ للتناقض والفساد وتكذيب العيان .
The proofs: and when this is established, all the contingent events and needs that are for the contingent (al-hadith) are established for that origin, since it [the origin] becomes susceptible to perishing and annihilation. And that also is necessary for the Qaramitah who make it eternal, even though they say: it was after it had not been, by origination (ibda'). And there is no power except by God. And the proof of ignorance [is that] what is in it potentially is prevented [from knowledge]? by the states of what is in it, of it, and what will be, mentioned from ignorance of sperms and seeds and others. So likewise it is necessary in hyle and clay and what they said. And it is necessary that they have no governance [of their claim], nor was anything from that by it. But if it [the claim] is, then it is prevented? from knowledge of what will be, so it makes its origin potentially manifested, appearing actually by what is made for it of materials and places by which it grows in that statement of tawhid, and that He [God] is the originator of all that so that everything that will be exists according to what they said, or that He is the creator of everything that will be eternally as He wills to be from origins and beginnings, or how He wills according to what the people of tawhid say. And since God, exalted, is able to create an origin in which everything is manifested potentially, He is able to originate everything as He wills without potential manifestation nor actual emergence, but rather by estimation and creation (al-taqdir wa al-takwin). And if they claim that things were in the origin hidden in their substance and then appear actually, that also returns to what we said, because that is their saying concerning sperms and seeds, along with what in this the intellect can refute by that which does not allow the existence of multiples/weaknesses? of a thing in its substance, due to contradiction, corruption, and the falsification of direct observation.
Source pages p. 663

Commentary
This passage is a continuation of the argument, now establishing tawhid by showing that the Qaramitah view leads to absurdities, and affirming God's direct creation. The author begins by stating that once the previous proof (the neediness and contingency of the world) is established, then all the contingent events and needs we observe are proven to belong to that original contingent substrate. Since that substrate is susceptible to perishing, the Qaramitah cannot claim it is eternal even if they say it was originated (ibda'). Their claim that the first originated being contains all things potentially actually prevents knowledge of future states, because potentiality is unknown. The same reasoning applies to hyle and clay (tina). Consequently, their claim has no governance, and if it did, it would preclude knowledge of what will be. The correct view, according to the people of tawhid, is that God is the originator of everything, creating each thing directly as He wills, without any pre-existent potentiality. God is able to create an origin containing everything potentially, but He is also able to create each thing individually as He wills, through estimation (taqdir) and creation (takwin). Finally, the author refutes the claim that things preexist hidden in a substance and then appear: this reduces to the same argument as with sperms and seeds, and reason rejects it because it implies contradictory states (multiple potentials in one substance), which contradicts both reason and direct observation.

Key Terms
الإبداع (ibda')
القوة (quwwa)
القرامطة (al-Qaramitah)
الهيولى (hayula)
الطينة (al-tina)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Qaramitah model that an eternal first being contains all things potentially is compatible with tawhid.
Correction: Maturidi shows that potentiality leads to ignorance and contingency, so the origin cannot be eternal; only direct creation by God is consistent with tawhid.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, why does the Qaramitah view of an eternal origin with potentiality fail?
A) Because potentiality implies that the origin is not originated.
B) Because potentiality leads to ignorance of future states, as seen in sperms and seeds.
C) Because the origin cannot be eternal if it contains potentiality.
D) Because the Qaramitah deny the existence of hyle and clay.

Key Takeaway
The Qaramitah model of an eternal origin with potentiality is refuted because potentiality implies ignorance, contradicting the idea of a knowable, governed creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You trust in potential—your plans, your abilities, your future. But the passage warns that potentiality without God's governance leads to ignorance. Where in your life have you assumed that because something has potential, you can know its outcome without relying on the Creator? Will you repent of that subtle self-reliance today?
?
The Qaramitah held to a philosophy that seemed logical—yet it obscured their knowledge of God. Are there theological or philosophical ideas you cling to that sound sensible but actually blind you to the majesty and knowledge of Allah? Are you willing to abandon them even if they are comfortable?
?
The passage concludes that their claim lacks 'governance' (تدبير). Do you live as if every detail of your existence is under God's direct governance, or do you act as if some things are left to blind potential? What would it look like to truly believe 'لا قوة إلا بالله' in your next decision?

Affirmation of Direct Creation and Final Refutation
Maturidi affirms direct creation and refutes hidden substance model.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi affirms that God creates directly by estimation and creation (al-taqdir wa al-takwin), and why the alternative model of things hidden in a substance is rationally impossible.

Core Idea
God creates each thing as He wills, without pre-existent potential or actual emergence.

Having refuted the Qaramitah model of potentiality, Maturidi now presents the correct understanding of tawhid: God's direct creation. He asserts that God is able to create things individually without relying on any pre-existing potential. He also refutes the claim that things preexist hidden in a substance, showing it leads to contradiction.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Notice the shift from refutation to positive affirmation.
This passage contains the core positive doctrine.
2
Identify the two possibilities
Maturidi contrasts two possibilities: either everything emerges from a potential-laden origin, or God creates directly. Identify the one he affirms.
Look for 'بالتقدير والتكوين' (estimation and creation).
3
Understand the refutation of hidden substance
Analyze the argument against things being hidden in a substance. Maturidi says it reduces to the same problem as sperms and seeds, and reason rejects it due to contradiction and falsification of observation.
This refutation uses logical impossibility.
4
Reflect on tawhid
Conclude that the proper tawhid is that God creates each thing directly as He wills, without any intermediate potentiality.
This affirms God's absolute power and knowledge.

Checkpoint
What is the proper method of creation according to Maturidi in this passage?
A) By bringing things out of a hidden potential in a primordial substance.
B) By estimation and creation (al-taqdir wa al-takwin) without any potential or actual emergence.
C) By a process of emanation from a first principle.
D) By using pre-existing materials and shaping them.

Key Takeaway
God's direct creation by estimation and creation is the only coherent model of tawhid; any model involving pre-existent potential or hidden substances is rationally impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that God creates everything directly, or do you secretly assume that some things 'just happen' through natural processes independent of His immediate will? What in your daily life—your reactions, worries, or thanks—reveals your actual belief? Will you today consciously attribute every small event to His direct creation?
?
When you witness the growth of a plant or the development of a fetus, do you attribute it to inherent potentials in matter, or do you see it as God's direct act of creation at every moment? How would your gratitude and reliance on Him change if you truly saw His hand in every detail?
?
The passage states that any model involving pre-existent potential is contradictory and falsified by observation. Are there areas in your understanding of the world where you unconsciously accept contradictory explanations—like attributing some outcomes to luck, chance, or nature? How does this lesson challenge you to purify your tawhid and live with complete trust in God's sole creativity?
